## Text Elements
Systen Design Problem Statement ^jyhQujN4

Problem Description  ^MGZUVv2D

Requirements ^Q81684Nb

Non Functional Requirements ^o1BPHki6

Back of the Envelope Estimations ^D1t8FijJ

Functional Requirements ^0wiEtg3U

Storage Requirements ^TljJbjLT

Daily Active Users(DAU) ^xp2fQE2W

API Routes ^pG2xYfY5

DataBase Model ^0ME7hiYp

High Level Design ^axodlEIN

Functional requirements define the specific features, abilities, and behaviors a system needs to have in order to fulfill its purpose. 
These requirements describe what the system should do and how users should use it. ^iBe4Nut4

Non-functional requirements refer to the qualities or characteristics a system should have, rather than specific functionalities. 
These requirements typically cover areas like performance, reliability, scalability, security, and usability. ^7MFlRu29

Use the whiteboard to list the 
system requirements in the 
'Requirements' box ^UlyHrua3

Use the whiteboard to provide 
an estimate of the Daily Active Users (DAU) and 
the system's storage requirements 
in the 'Estimations' box. ^CvXKAReo

Making back-of-the-envelope estimations is an essential step in system design interviews. It allows you to understand the scale of the system, which helps inform design decisions. 
Try to make realistic estimations, but remember that they don't need to be exact. ^dDHR6Pwr

Estimating DAU helps you understand the level of traffic the system will handle. 
Consider the application's purpose and its target audience to inform your estimate. ^fFynK00q

To estimate storage requirements consider user data, transactional data, log data, and backups. 
Remember to also consider the data growth rate. ^PH77wkAn

CAP Theorem ^xnNy71LI

Given the constraints of the CAP theorem, 
where would you place the emphasis for your 
system: consistency or availability? Justify your answer. ^LLC7w6Q0

CAP Theorem states that a distributed system can't provide 
Consistency, Availability, and Partition tolerance all at once. ^cbMphzjA

Consistency ^b1EAdync

Every read receives the most recent write or an error. All nodes in the system see the same data at the same time. ^EeAm0zSa

Availability ^RdJMoUEF


Every request gets a non-error response, without guarantee it contains the most recent write. 
All nodes are always operational for read and write operations. ^pJkCTpdj

Partition Tolerance ^OsuS4JXF

The system continues to function despite network partitions, even if split into sub-systems 
unable to communicate. ^lDIVWNVE

All distributed systems must be partition tolerant by default. Your task in the interview is to choose between Consistency (CP system) and Availability (AP system), based on the systems requirement. ^nPVQqOpy

You should start a system design interview by clarifying the requirements, ensuring alignment between you and the interviewer. 
Requirements should be broken down into functional and non-functional requirements. ^7kRLPn9t

Use the whiteboard to diagram 
the major components of the system in the box 
labeled 'High-Level Design' ^UVNPszRq

When providing a high-level overview of the major system components, diagram each component with arrows indicating the flow of data. ^IZDIAaKc

Core Components ^sxhBqkRk

What are the core components needed for the system's main logic? ^y1GIvq4y

Data Storage ^wcBOjhdb

What kind of database best suits this system? ^uoKZa6DC

Scaling ^OnmPoujL

What components are needed to scale the system? ie. load balancers, message queues, and caches. ^b5BW3ucW

Use the whiteboard to document the 
API endpoints that your system will have. 
Include request, response, and 
the purpose of each endpoint ^GYB7AM60

API design involves mapping out the endpoints your system will need. For each endpoint, consider its request, response, and purpose. ^KeMaP4HS

Request ^3W5rj0gy

Identify what data the API would need to perform its task. This could include parameters in the URL, the HTTP method used, or data sent in the body of the request. ^2rOuMU3l

Response ^hZTXP8RS

Determine what the API will return after performing its task. This can include status codes, headers, and response body content. ^lUgjMIhB

Purpose ^7wQRBJWw

Describe the function of the API endpoint within the system. What does it do and why is it needed? ^KK9LYeK6

API Design ^wE5hdAzR

Major Component ^tmfRX7Bl

Major Component ^1gnskZpS

API Design ^DHrjglby

What type of database would you use for the 
system and why? ^kyAQ879w

Choosing a database involves understanding the nature of your data, the required operations, and aligning this choice with the system's requirements. 
Always make sure to justify your decision and weigh the trade-offs in the interview. ^S1EuYOx5

Relational Databases ^Ki4FFsDE

Use for structured data and when relations matter significantly. ie. MySQL or PostgreSQL. ^RhqR5F9h

NoSQL Databases ^hLKgXzcP

Choose for large volumes of unstructured data or when read/write speed is crucial. ie. MongoDB or Cassandra. ^Kgsk8k8i

Use the whiteboard to sketch 
the database schema by writing 
inside the 'Database Schema' box ^jWJh2TkT

DataBase Schema ^NigrIgqb

Database schema design involves identifying main entities, their attributes, and relationships. Aim for a balance between efficient storage and query performance. ^YjMIJssk

Identify Entities & Attributes ^kw48M39A

Each entity corresponds to a table or collection. Define the attributes of each entity, which become fields or columns. ^1FsNHi3u

Define Relationships ^lSauuZdd

Consider normalization to minimize data redundancy, but be aware that denormalization may sometimes boost performance.
 ^qlG1HgQF

Consider the relationships between entities, which could be one-to-one, one-to-many, or many-to-many. ^6pyMtZLp

Balance Efficiency & Performance ^Xl3Hq8JG

How would you handle data availability, 
replication, and synchronization? ^L2Fjezmg

Handling data availability, replication, and synchronization is crucial for distributed systems. 
Consider the following when discussing your data model in an interview. ^b7Hwz3CK

Data Availability ^rD1WJE3C

Consider redundant storage, frequent backups, or using services with built-in redundancy like 
AWS S3 or Google Cloud Storage. ^QnfoR7Zm

Data Replication ^iJZmUZ0K

Choose a replication methodology, like master-slave or peer-to-peer, 
and a fitting replication strategy (synchronous or asynchronous) based on your system's needs. ^j7OaTmLu

Data Synchronization ^j6w0KfWi

Consider using a consensus algorithm like Paxos or Raft in a distributed system for synchronization. ^Uz8WtY8B

DataBase Replication ^VkudGQPT

Understand the Requirements ^URvtFWTi

Requirements ^PFG99Dmt

Back of the Envelope Estimations ^lGAxOuwV

CAP Theorem ^POxEyU6T

Data Model ^GagmcJsd

Database Type ^H1tsaRXE

DataBase Schema ^RSZZEeWM

DataBase Replication ^lIP8TCx9

Component 1 ^uMzHkJjM

Component 3 ^VCjkS7uV

Scalability ^tjtoYBUg

Scaling ^HBevW0PI

BottleNecks ^yU95vFPS

System Assessments ^PqpTFsjL

Security ^3oRMoiiB

Monitoring ^5sW6w7tF

Testing ^NpuEQBo3

How would you ensure the system can scale to 
support the number of users you estimated 
in the back-of-the-envelope estimation? ^7jxVOQMA

Scaling strategies should align with estimated load and growth. Different parts of the system may require different scaling strategies. ^W15nhDgH

Horizontal & Vertical Scaling ^8pglsxyW

Horizontal scaling adds more machines, while vertical scaling increases the capacity of an existing machine. ^lJPw9HSx

Load Balancing ^3ILMJq8W

Distributes the workload evenly among servers, 
enhancing efficiency and reliability. ^dSb3nScv

Data Partitioning & Caching ^rCAo881P

Data partitioning manages large databases more efficiently. Caching enhances performance by storing frequently accessed data. ^yxh9rvnI

Can you identify a significant bottleneck in the system 
and explain how you would mitigate it? ^xKg3jsZG

Consider different parts of the system for potential bottlenecks, such as the database, network, application server, or user interface. Then, discuss mitigation strategies and their effects on the system. ^fkFTjwXC

Identifying Bottleneck ^Pr9AM4AU

Pick a potential bottleneck that could have a major impact on the system's performance. ^GHua9Wwu

Mitigating Bottleneck ^lqVg1ANp

Describe strategies for mitigation like system scaling, code optimization, improving database queries, or modifying system architecture ^vmQo0ZBX

Considering Effects ^t2PFZy40

Remember to consider the effects of your mitigation strategies on the rest of the system. ^KNaX2tow

Identify 1-2 key security measures you would 
implement in the system and provide an explanation of 
how they would be applied? ^iFclJh0q

Consider critical security aspects like user data protection, secure access controls, network security, or secure coding practices. Choose 1-2 measures that are crucial for your system and describe their implementation and impact on system security. ^HMvDYFQ1

Identifying Security Measures ^PcaIOvF1

Identify 1-2 key security measures critical to your system's security. These could be user data encryption, secure access controls, network security measures, or secure coding practices. ^ytXXGGRH

Implementing Security Measures ^9In56t2X

Describe how you would implement these measures in your system, explaining their function and how they enhance your system's security. ^qaUoooXn

How would you monitor the system for 
performance and issues? ^SkEyOC7M

Identify 1-2 key performance aspects critical to your system such as response time, throughput, error rates, etc. Explain how you would monitor these specific metrics through the use of specific tools, real-time analytics, alerts, or log reviews. ^DAGm9E5R

Identifying Performance Metrics ^4Dnbri2m

Pick 1-2 key performance metrics crucial to your system's smooth operation. These could be response time, throughput, error rates, or others. ^pdSDcST9

Monitoring Performance Metrics ^KCgY5fyD

Explain how you would monitor these chosen metrics. This might involve specific tools, real-time analytics, alerts, or regular log reviews. ^2lM27bBU

What key aspects of the system would you focus on 
when testing for functionality and reliability, and 
what testing strategies would you use for these aspects? ^Vpju0N49

Identify the critical components of your system and the relevant testing strategies for these components. The strategies might include unit testing for individual functions, load testing for scalability components, or integration testing for complex interactions. ^ln3t6IpF

Identifying Key Components ^gfXe8DKh

Focus on the critical components of your system that demand rigorous testing to ensure functionality and reliability. ^axKZ8fzE

Applying Testing Strategies ^VgwHzdSZ

Describe the testing strategies suitable for these components. These might include unit, load, or integration testing. ^fanmjdfL
